  61. I've bought two of these so far and have just finished my first tub (after about 6 months!) and have been really happy with the results. A big mistake I made when I first used this product was using too much and not spreading it enough. The best way to use this product is to, using your index finger, pull out a small amount (the material is very thick) and spread it into both of your hands. The consistency will feel very sticky, but once put into your damp to dry hair (depending on how much shine you want), it comes out completely matte. Be sure to spread it evenly throughout as much of your hair as you want control over and let the product do its work. The hold is really intense - I can have it in for a day, sleep in with it, and still have some residual hold into the next day. It does come out rather easily in the shower with or without shampoo. If you want some shine, you can put more into your hair and it will start to look very slick (I found this out by mistake). In summary - good hold, great for disconnected undercuts.<br /><br />Now half the reason I'm writing this review is to compare it to the American Crew equivalent (by product description: high hold/low shine) Fiber. I (dumbly) forgot my second tub of TIGI Bed Head at home and couldn't find the product in any stores nearby. I couldn't find a straight review comparing the two products anywhere in my cursory search so, here's a tip. The American Crew is much less sticky right off the bat, it comes out feeling more like a modern day wax/pomade than a hardcore clay. It definitely doesn't give the hold that the TIGI gives, and looks a bit more greasy. However, if the TIGI is a 5 star the American Crew would be a 3.5-4 star.

Why change?? Probably because most people using this stuff don't know and don't care about lathering your head everyday with carcinogenic and endocrine disrupting chemicals. They just care how nice their hair looks. Can't blame them, though...&#34;Nice hair is one of those intrinsically worthwhile pursuits&#34;--Aristotle.<br /><br />Anyway, check out EWG's cosmetic database for a list of the potential carcinogens in this product. It scores a 6 out of 10, 10 being the worst. Most popular hair care products are in the 8-9 range...I bet the old formulation was more in the 4-5 range.<br /><br />Will I buy it again? Idk...I think I'll experiment with the less toxic hair care products. If they suck, then I'll go back to this.ange.<br /><br />Will I buy it again? I usually dry until my hair is at the &#34;almost completely dry&#34; point but still has a little cold/wetness feeling in it.<br />5) I take 2 fingertips worth of product, and rub generously between my hands to heat it up and evenly distribute it.<br />6) Starting at the top of my head, I apply the product in circular motions making sure to spread it across my roots to the tips of my hairs.<br />7) Once the product is fully applied (no excess product left in hair and all parts of hair have been covered), I use a comb to slick my hair back.<br />Tip: Give this product a few minutes to &#34;settle&#34; in your hair. The water in your hair needs to dry out, until then it could change shape if you're moving your head a lot. Once it's dry, I haven't had it deform my hair.<br /><br />If my hair is too wet and I apply this product, I find that it won't hold as well and will often deform my hair as the water dries in my hair, which gets annoying. So my advice: find the right amount of wetness your hair needs to be at before applying this product. Let me preface this by saying I LOVE this product (as do many others).<br /><br />For a long time I was searching high and low for a product that would hold my super-thick hair, and not leave it looking like I dipped my head in Crisco.   449. Where shall one begin with the pitfalls of this product?<br /><br />In no particular order of concern it is important to note that once the item has been sitting around for the duration of a month (despite regular use), the wax begins to harden along the outside and soften on the inside within its closed container. In that predicament, what you may have is a can of dried up Elmer's glue. Granted, the wax smells better than Elmer's glue but the adhesive properties are still there.<br /><br />If used in the morning (or any time of day, I just happen to use it in the morning) at a small dime-sized amount, this wax leaves a sticky residue on your hair, hands, the container, and whatever else you may touch (perhaps your faucet, sink, or towel as you may try to wash off the wax from your hands). Removing the residue from one's hands requires anywhere between 2 to 5 minutes of work under warm water and soap.<br /><br />Once the wax is applied onto your hair (post towel-drying) and it is styled to your preferences (so long as it does not try to defy gravity too much), the hold remains for the duration of the day. When the wetness of your hair disappears sometime later, the last thing you may want to touch is your own scalp. For the purposes of imagery, hair on your head will feel akin to combing your hand inside dried-up rice pudding or dried-up oatmeal (assuming your hair is very thick, which mine is). If at any time, you touch your hair to perhaps alter the style, or fix a mistake you did not catch earlier, your hands once again have a sticky residue that is very troublesome to get rid off.<br /><br />At the end of the day, it is not at all wise to leave the wax remaining on your head while sleeping but sometimes we as humans forget. If the wax if left on your scalp and you have very thick hair, you wake up to a mirror and you can see your sleeping patterns. I am a side-sleeper and it is evident as I woke up with a lob-sided mohawk after I accidentally forgot to wash out the wax from my hair. After leaving the wax in your hair for an extended period of time and accidentally sleeping in it, your hair must be washed thoroughly because it is very difficult to control if the scalp is just washed with water then slowly dried with a towel. Not to mention it's a time-consuming process.<br /><br />Whenever I walked into a salon to get my hair trimmed, the cosmetologist always looks disgusted at how unpleasant my hair is to touch. It looks nice but no stylist dares to touch it until it the wax is washed off. Both times, I am handed off to an assistant who washes off the wax completely before even touching my hair with bare hands. Both times were such an embarrassing ordeal. In one instance of an intimate encounter I was cuddling next to someone and my hair brushed against her skin. Her words were not at all reassuring. My hair looks great, but she mentions ... &#34;do not go anywhere near it&#34;.<br /><br />Bottom line, this product is more drama than I could ever want. It is not worth the extra hassle in the morning, the glue-like texture, the residue, the disgust, let alone it's price for all the downfalls. My hair looks great even in high humidity but I will look for something with less maintenance.the wax from my hair. For TIGI Matter separation wax, here's the breakdown:<br /><br />What's the \\"actual\\" hold like? Pretty good.<br /><br />How easy is it to work into the hair? Moderate. This product is thicker and denser than most other products; however, unlike Fiber (with the wet sand feel), this product is still very creamy - thus it's still easy to spread into the hair.<br /><br />How natural does the hair feel throughout the day? Hair quickly develops a thick, slightly-sticky and sandy texture.<br /><br />Is the hold consistent? Yes; however, the sacrifice is that the hair will not feel quite as natural.<br /><br />How much do you need to get a decent hold? An average amount.<br /><br />Does it wash out easily? Not exactly. As the hair becomes harder throughout the day, it becomes slightly more difficult to wash out. To be fair, though, this product is still much easier to wash out than the clay-ish products like Grunge Mat or Molding Clay.<br /><br />How does it smell? Almost no smell with a few subtle floral notes.<br /><br />Please see my other reviews to compare against all of the above products. I personally like this slightly more than Fiber - as the hold strong and it's easy to work into the hair. The only downside is that your hair will start to feel slightly sticky and sandy several hours after application. This can probably be curbed if you use a lesser amount; however, if you have thick hair, be prepared to experience this downside.bably be curbed if you use a lesser amount; however, if you have thick hair, be prepared to experience this downside.
